</ul></span></p><hr><h1 id="01-programming">01 Programming</h1><h2 id="01-programming-net">NET</h2><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should you still target netstandard?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When you need to support older runtime families that cannot consume modern <code>netX</code> libraries.<br>
If all consumers are modern .NET, target <code>net8.0</code> instead.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/NET Standart.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/NET Standart.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">NET Standart</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the pragmatic default for new libraries today?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Target the modern runtime you run in production.<br>
Add multi targeting only when you have a concrete consumer requirement.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/NET Standart.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/NET Standart.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">NET Standart</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>ASP.NET Web API</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is mapping, why is it needed, and how can it be implemented?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Mapping is the transformation of data from one shape/type to another (for example, Domain Entity -&gt; DTO -&gt; API response model).<br>
It is used to decouple layers, hide internal details, enforce API contracts, prevent over-posting, and shape data for clients.<br>
Typical implementation options:</p>
<ul>
<li dir="auto">manual mapping (constructors, factory methods, extension methods)</li>
<li dir="auto">mapping libraries (AutoMapper, Mapster)</li>
<li dir="auto">code generation / source generators for mappings<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ASP.NET Web API</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What are serialization and deserialization?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Serialization converts an in-memory object graph into a format that can be stored or transmitted (for example, JSON text or a binary payload).<br>
Deserialization is the reverse process: converting that stored/transmitted representation back into objects.<br>
Common uses: API payloads, persistence, caching, messaging.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ASP.NET Web API</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is JSON and why is it used?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">JSON (JavaScript Object Notation) is a lightweight text data format based on objects (name/value pairs) and arrays.<br>
It is widely used for data interchange, especially in HTTP APIs, because it is human-readable, language-agnostic, and easy to parse.<br>
In .NET, JSON is commonly handled with <code>System.Text.Json</code> (built-in) or Newtonsoft.Json.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ASP.NET Web API</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Where should authentication and authorization live in an ASP.NET Core API?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Put authentication and authorization in the pipeline so endpoints can assume an authenticated principal.<br>
Use middleware for auth and use endpoint metadata and policies to decide access per endpoint.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ASP.NET Web API</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When do you choose middleware over an endpoint filter?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Choose middleware for cross-cutting concerns that apply broadly (logging, auth, exception handling).<br>
Choose endpoint filters for endpoint scoped behavior and validation around Minimal APIs.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/ASP.NET Web API.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ASP.NET Web API</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is middleware in ASP.NET Core?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Middleware is a component in the HTTP request pipeline. It can inspect/modify the request and response, call the next component, or short-circuit the pipeline (for example, return a cached response without calling the next middleware). Order matters.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Middlewares</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Action filter vs middleware: what is the difference?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Middleware is pipeline-level and can apply to all requests (before routing/MVC, around endpoint execution). Action filters are MVC-level and run only for MVC actions, with access to action context, model binding, and results; they are a better fit for cross-cutting concerns that are specific to controller actions.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Middlewares</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How can you log execution time for all requests?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use a middleware that measures elapsed time around <code>next()</code> and logs it (or an action filter if you only care about MVC actions).</p>
<pre class="language-csharp"><code class="language-csharp is-loaded">app<span class="token punctuation">.</span><span class="token function">Use</span><span class="token punctuation">(</span><span class="token keyword">async</span> <span class="token punctuation">(</span>ctx<span class="token punctuation">,</span> next<span class="token punctuation">)</span> <span class="token operator">=&gt;</span>
<span class="token punctuation">{</span>
    <span class="token class-name"><span class="token keyword">var</span></span> sw <span class="token operator">=</span> System<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Diagnostics<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Stopwatch<span class="token punctuation">.</span><span class="token function">StartNew</span><span class="token punctuation">(</span><span class="token punctuation">)</span><span class="token punctuation">;</span>
    <span class="token keyword">try</span>
    <span class="token punctuation">{</span>
        <span class="token keyword">await</span> <span class="token function">next</span><span class="token punctuation">(</span><span class="token punctuation">)</span><span class="token punctuation">;</span>
    <span class="token punctuation">}</span>
    <span class="token keyword">finally</span>
    <span class="token punctuation">{</span>
        sw<span class="token punctuation">.</span><span class="token function">Stop</span><span class="token punctuation">(</span><span class="token punctuation">)</span><span class="token punctuation">;</span>
        app<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Logger<span class="token punctuation">.</span><span class="token function">LogInformation</span><span class="token punctuation">(</span><span class="token string">"{Method} {Path} -&gt; {StatusCode} in {ElapsedMs} ms"</span><span class="token punctuation">,</span>
            ctx<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Request<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Method<span class="token punctuation">,</span>
            ctx<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Request<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Path<span class="token punctuation">,</span>
            ctx<span class="token punctuation">.</span>Response<span class="token punctuation">.</span>StatusCode<span class="token punctuation">,</span>
            sw<span class="token punctuation">.</span>ElapsedMilliseconds<span class="token punctuation">)</span><span class="token punctuation">;</span>
    <span class="token punctuation">}</span>
<span class="token punctuation">}</span><span class="token punctuation">)</span><span class="token punctuation">;</span>
</code><button class="copy-code-button"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-copy"><rect x="8" y="8" width="14" height="14" rx="2" ry="2"></rect><path d="M4 16c-1.1 0-2-.9-2-2V4c0-1.1.9-2 2-2h10c1.1 0 2 .9 2 2"></path></svg></button></pre>
<p dir="auto"><em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Middlewares</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How can you centrally catch errors for all requests?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Add a global exception-handling middleware. In ASP.NET Core this is commonly done with <code>app.UseExceptionHandler(...)</code> (and <code>app.UseDeveloperExceptionPage()</code> in development). The handler can log the exception and return a consistent error response (for example, RFC 7807 Problem Details).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Middlewares</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the ASP.NET request processing pipeline?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A request is received by the host (for example, Kestrel) and then flows through an ordered chain of middleware. Middleware can add features (routing, authN/authZ, CORS, compression, etc.), select an endpoint, and finally execute the endpoint (MVC action, Minimal API handler, etc.). On the way back out, the middleware chain unwinds, allowing post-processing of the response.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Middlewares</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is an action filter?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">An MVC filter (for example, implementing <code>IActionFilter</code>/<code>IAsyncActionFilter</code>) that runs before and/or after a controller action executes. It can validate inputs, modify the action arguments, short-circuit by setting a result, or wrap execution to implement cross-cutting concerns such as logging, caching, and metrics.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/ASP.NET Web API/Middlewares.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Middlewares</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>CSharp</h3><h4>Concurrency and Parallelism</h4><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between concurrency and parallelism in practice?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Concurrency is about responsiveness and non-blocking progress, often with async I/O.<br>
Parallelism is about throughput for CPU-bound workloads by using multiple cores simultaneously.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Concurrency and Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why do many production outages in .NET systems look like "performance" but are actually concurrency bugs?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because thread starvation, deadlocks, lock contention, and unbounded fan-out all manifest as latency spikes and timeouts before obvious crashes.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Concurrency and Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the first decision before choosing a primitive (<code>Task</code>, <code>lock</code>, <code>Parallel</code>, <code>Channel</code>)?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Classify the workload as I/O-bound vs CPU-bound and define cancellation/error boundaries. Primitive choice follows that classification.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Concurrency and Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">You need to call 300 external APIs in one request and cut latency. Why is unbounded <code>Task.WhenAll</code> often a bad first choice?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because it can overload downstream dependencies, saturate connection pools, and create timeout storms. Bounded fan-out keeps latency gains while preserving system stability.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Concurrency and Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">For one requirement ("update shared state safely"), when do you choose <code>lock</code> vs <code>SemaphoreSlim</code> vs <code>Channel&lt;T&gt;</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use <code>lock</code> for short synchronous sections, <code>SemaphoreSlim</code> for async flows that need awaiting, and <code>Channel&lt;T&gt;</code> when you also need queueing, ordering, or backpressure.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Concurrency and Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Concurrency and Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How is asynchrony different from multithreading?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Asynchrony is about not blocking while waiting (especially for I/O). An <code>async</code> method can release the current thread while awaiting, and continue later.<br>
Multithreading is about executing work on multiple threads concurrently (for example, for parallel CPU-bound work). Async code can be single-threaded and still be asynchronous.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Async Await.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Async Await.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Async Await</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between <code>Thread</code> and <code>Task</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>Thread</code> is an OS thread you manage directly (heavier, dedicated execution).<br>
<code>Task</code> is a higher-level abstraction representing an asynchronous operation or a unit of work, typically scheduled on the thread pool (and for I/O it may not require a dedicated thread while waiting).<br>
References: <a data-tooltip-position="top" aria-label="https://ru.stackoverflow.com/questions/548876/%D0%92-%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BC-%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0-%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D1%83-task-%D0%B8-thread-%D0%B8-%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B4%D0%B0-%D1%87%D1%82%D0%BE-%D0%BB%D1%83%D1%87%D1%88%D0%B5-%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C" rel="noopener nofollow" class="external-link" href="https://ru.stackoverflow.com/questions/548876/%D0%92-%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BC-%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%86%D0%B0-%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D1%83-task-%D0%B8-thread-%D0%B8-%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B4%D0%B0-%D1%87%D1%82%D0%BE-%D0%BB%D1%83%D1%87%D1%88%D0%B5-%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B7%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C" target="_blank">Difference between Task and Thread (ru StackOverflow)</a><br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Async Await.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Async Await.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Async Await</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between <code>await</code> and <code>Task.Result</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>await</code> waits asynchronously: it does not block the current thread and it unwraps exceptions.<br>
<code>Task.Result</code> waits synchronously: it blocks the current thread, can cause deadlocks under a <code>SynchronizationContext</code> (UI / legacy ASP.NET), and wraps exceptions in <code>AggregateException</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Async Await.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Async Await.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Async Await</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is <code>Task</code> not equivalent to a thread?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>Task</code> models completion and scheduling, while threads are execution resources. Many async tasks complete I/O without holding a thread during waiting.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Tasks.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Tasks.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Tasks</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should <code>Task.Run</code> be used in ASP.NET Core?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Rarely for request I/O. Mostly for CPU-bound work that must be isolated from the request thread, ideally with bounded concurrency.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Tasks.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Tasks.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Tasks</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is <code>Task.WhenAll</code> usually better than sequential <code>await</code> in independent calls?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">It allows overlap of independent waits, reducing total latency and preserving structured error aggregation.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Tasks.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Tasks.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Tasks</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is cancellation in .NET called cooperative?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because callee code chooses where to observe token state and terminate safely. Runtime does not forcibly kill the operation.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/CancellationToken.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/CancellationToken.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">CancellationToken</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Should canceled operations be logged as errors?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Usually no. They are expected control flow when initiated by caller timeout/user cancellation. Log at debug/info unless behavior is unexpected.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/CancellationToken.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/CancellationToken.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">CancellationToken</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When is it reasonable not to cancel immediately after token is signaled?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When a tiny critical section must complete to keep state consistent (for example finishing a single idempotent write or releasing resource ownership).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/CancellationToken.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/CancellationToken.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">CancellationToken</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why can adding more parallel workers reduce performance?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because of contention, synchronization overhead, cache misses, and context switching once you exceed useful core-level parallelism.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do you decide <code>MaxDegreeOfParallelism</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Start near <code>Environment.ProcessorCount</code>, then tune with workload benchmarks and production telemetry rather than assumptions.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should you avoid PLINQ?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When correctness depends on strict ordering, side-effect sequencing, or when query-level debugging clarity matters more than terse syntax.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Parallelism.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Parallelism.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Parallelism</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is ThreadPool starvation and how does it usually start?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Starvation means queued work cannot get workers quickly enough, often triggered by blocking waits on pool threads or unbounded CPU work.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/ThreadPool.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/ThreadPool.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ThreadPool</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why can an async app still suffer ThreadPool issues?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because only part of the call graph is async; any blocking segment on pool workers can throttle the entire system.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/ThreadPool.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/ThreadPool.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ThreadPool</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Is increasing <code>ThreadPool.SetMinThreads</code> a primary solution?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Usually no. It can mitigate symptoms but the primary fix is removing blocking and controlling workload concurrency.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/ThreadPool.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/ThreadPool.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ThreadPool</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does lock ordering prevent deadlocks?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A consistent acquisition order removes circular wait, which breaks one required deadlock condition.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Deadlocks.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Deadlocks.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Deadlocks</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Can async code deadlock without explicit <code>lock</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Yes. Blocking on async continuations (<code>.Result</code>/<code>.Wait</code>) under constrained synchronization contexts can create wait cycles.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Deadlocks.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Deadlocks.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Deadlocks</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a practical first response when production shows suspected deadlock?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Capture process dumps, inspect blocked/waiting stacks, identify owned monitors/semaphores, then enforce ordering or remove blocking boundaries.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Deadlocks.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Concurrency and Parallelism/Deadlocks.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Deadlocks</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h4>Fundamentals</h4><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Which access modifiers do you know?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>public</code>, <code>private</code>, <code>protected</code>, <code>internal</code>, <code>protected internal</code>, <code>private protected</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Fundamentals</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What are the default access modifiers for fields, methods, structs, and classes?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Fields and methods default to <code>private</code>. Top-level classes and structs default to <code>internal</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Fundamentals</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is implicit typing in C#?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">It's using <code>var</code> so the compiler infers the variable's static type from the initializer.<br>
<code>var</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Fundamentals</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a variable?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A variable is a named, typed storage location that holds a value (or a reference) so your program can read and update that value while it runs.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Fundamentals.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Fundamentals</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do you handle potential errors in code?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use <code>try</code>/<code>catch</code>/<code>finally</code> to handle exceptions and guarantee cleanup (often via <code>using</code>/<code>await using</code> for disposables).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Exception Handling.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Exception Handling.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Exception Handling</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When might <code>finally</code> not execute?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When the process terminates abruptly and normal stack unwinding doesn't happen (for example, crash/kill, <code>Environment.FailFast()</code>, or <code>StackOverflowException</code>).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Exception Handling.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Exception Handling.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Exception Handling</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What types can you use in <code>foreach</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Any type that implements <code>IEnumerable</code> / <code>IEnumerable&lt;T&gt;</code>, or any type that provides the enumerator pattern (<code>GetEnumerator()</code> + <code>Current</code> + <code>MoveNext()</code>).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Foreach.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Foreach.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Foreach</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How is <code>foreach</code> implemented under the hood?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">The compiler lowers it to enumerator code: call <code>GetEnumerator()</code>, loop <code>MoveNext()</code>, read <code>Current</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Foreach.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Foreach.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Foreach</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is <code>yield</code> and how does it work?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">It creates an iterator: each <code>yield return</code> produces a value and pauses the method; the method resumes on the next iteration request.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Foreach.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Foreach.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Foreach</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why might you need <code>ref</code> for reference types if reference types are already passed by reference?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Reference type <em>values</em> (the reference) are passed by value. <code>ref</code> is needed when you want the callee to replace the caller's reference (rebind it to a different object).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Methods</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is an <code>in</code> parameter used for?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">To pass an argument by readonly reference: avoid copies for large structs and communicate that the method should not modify the argument.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Methods</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What are optional parameters in methods?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Parameters with default values that callers can omit; the default is substituted at compile time at the call site.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Methods</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">In a hierarchy where <code>Animal a = new Dog();</code>, how can you make <code>a.Category()</code> return the derived value, and what does that imply for API design?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Mark the base member as <code>virtual</code> and the derived member as <code>override</code>. That enables polymorphic dispatch by runtime type. It also means the base API explicitly supports extensibility and behavioral substitution.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Methods</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should you prefer <code>new</code> over <code>override</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Prefer <code>new</code> only when polymorphism is not desired and you intentionally want different behavior based on the compile-time reference type (for compatibility or specialized APIs). In most extensible designs, <code>override</code> is the safer default.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Methods</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">A base method is not marked <code>virtual</code>, but you need derived-specific behavior. What are your options?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Option 1: Change the base API to <code>virtual</code> (best if you own the base type and want polymorphism). Option 2: Hide with <code>new</code> (works, but no polymorphism and can confuse callers). Option 3: Redesign with composition/strategy if inheritance is not a good fit.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Methods.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Methods</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a namespace? Why do we need it?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A namespace groups related types and avoids name collisions; it also helps organize large projects.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Namespaces.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Namespaces.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Namespaces</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is reflection?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Runtime inspection of assemblies, types, members, and attributes (via <code>System.Reflection</code>), sometimes also used to invoke members dynamically.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Reflection.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Reflection.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Reflection</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is an attribute and why do we need it?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">An attribute is metadata attached to code. It can be discovered (often via reflection) and used by frameworks/tools to drive behavior (serialization, DI, validation, routing, tests, etc.).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Reflection.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Reflection.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Reflection</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is <code>List&lt;T&gt;</code> generally preferred over old non-generic collections like <code>ArrayList</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>List&lt;T&gt;</code> gives compile-time type safety, avoids most casts, and prevents boxing for value types like <code>int</code>, which usually improves performance and correctness.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Generics.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Generics.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Generics</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">You wrote <code>T Parse&lt;T&gt;(string input)</code> and need to call <code>TryParse</code> inside. What should you change?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Add an abstraction or constraint-based strategy because unconstrained <code>T</code> has no guaranteed static parse API. In modern C#, static-abstract interface members can model this cleanly; otherwise pass a parser delegate.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Generics.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Generics.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Generics</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When can adding a <code>where T : class</code> constraint be a design smell?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When it is used only to make null handling easy. If the API should support value types too, this constraint blocks valid use cases and reduces reusability.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Generics.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Generics.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Generics</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h5>Types</h5><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the practical difference between value-type and reference-type assignment?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Value-type assignment copies the value itself. Reference-type assignment copies the reference to the same object.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Types</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Do value types always live on the stack and reference types always on the heap?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">No. Storage location depends on context (local, field, captured variable, boxing), not only on the type category.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Types</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When does boxing happen, and why is it expensive?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Boxing happens when a value type is converted to <code>object</code> or an interface. It allocates on the heap and adds copy/GC overhead.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Types</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why must <code>Equals</code> and <code>GetHashCode</code> be consistent?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Hash-based collections rely on the contract: equal objects must produce equal hash codes, otherwise lookups can fail.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Types</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do you choose between <code>class</code>, <code>struct</code>, and <code>record</code> in C#?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use <code>class</code> for identity/reference semantics, <code>struct</code> for small immutable value-like data, and <code>record</code> for data models with value-based equality and concise syntax.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/CSharp/Fundamentals/Types/Types.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Types</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does passing a reference type by value still allow mutation of the object?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because the copied value is the reference itself, and both references still target the same object instance.<br>
