<p dir="auto">A standard way to implement <code>IDisposable</code> so both explicit cleanup (<code>Dispose()</code>) and (optionally) finalization are supported.<br>
Typical shape: <code>Dispose()</code> calls <code>Dispose(true)</code> and then <code>GC.SuppressFinalize(this)</code>; a finalizer (if needed) calls <code>Dispose(false)</code>; <code>Dispose(bool disposing)</code> releases unmanaged resources and, when <code>disposing</code> is true, also disposes managed fields.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/Runtime/Memory Leaks.md" href="Software Engineering/01 Programming/NET/Runtime/Memory Leaks.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Memory Leaks</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h1 id="02-computer-science">02 Computer Science</h1><h2 id="02-computer-science-algorithms">Algorithms</h2><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is an algorithm? How is its efficiency measured?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">An algorithm is a step-by-step procedure to solve a problem. Its efficiency is measured by time and space complexity, typically using Big-O to describe growth with input size.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Algorithms.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Algorithms.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Algorithms</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>Disjoint Set</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is path compression?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">During find(x), path compression rewires nodes on the path from x to the root to point directly to the root. This flattens the tree over time and makes future operations faster.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Disjoint Set/Disjoint Set Union-Find.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Disjoint Set/Disjoint Set Union-Find.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Disjoint Set Union-Find</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>Graph Algorithms</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should I use BFS vs DFS?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use BFS when you need shortest paths in an unweighted graph or level-order exploration. Use DFS for reachability, cycle detection, topological sorting, and when you want to explore one path deeply (often with recursion/stack).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Graph Algorithms/DFS BFS.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Graph Algorithms/DFS BFS.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">DFS BFS</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does Dijkstra require non-negative weights?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">The algorithm is greedy: once a vertex is extracted as the current minimum, its distance is assumed final. Negative edges can later produce a shorter path to an already-finalized vertex, so the greedy step becomes incorrect (use Bellman-Ford for graphs with negative edges).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Graph Algorithms/Dijkstra.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Graph Algorithms/Dijkstra.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Dijkstra</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>Sorting Algorithms</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is Bubble Sort?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Bubble sort repeatedly swaps adjacent out-of-order elements, pushing large values toward the end each pass. It is easy to understand but rarely used in production due to poor performance.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Bubble Sort.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Bubble Sort.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Bubble Sort</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is Insertion Sort?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Insertion sort grows a sorted prefix by inserting each next element into its correct position. It is fast for small inputs and nearly-sorted data, and it is a common building block inside hybrid sorts.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Insertion Sort.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Insertion Sort.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Insertion Sort</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is Quick Sort?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Quick sort partitions the array around a pivot so smaller elements go left and larger go right, then recursively sorts the partitions. It is often very fast in practice but has a worst-case O(n^2) if pivots are consistently bad.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Quick Sort.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Quick Sort.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Quick Sort</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is Selection Sort?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Selection sort builds a sorted prefix by repeatedly selecting the minimum remaining element and swapping it into place. It does a predictable number of comparisons but is still quadratic time.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Selection Sort.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Selection Sort.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Selection Sort</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is Merge Sort?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Merge sort is a divide-and-conquer algorithm: split the array, sort each half, then merge the two sorted halves. It has reliable O(n log n) time and is stable, at the cost of extra memory.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Merge Sort.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/Sorting Algorithms/Merge Sort.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Merge Sort</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>String Searching</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What does the prefix function (LPS) represent?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">For each position in the pattern, it stores the length of the longest proper prefix that is also a suffix ending at that position. This lets KMP shift the pattern without losing valid partial matches.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/String Searching/KMP (Knuth-Morris-Pratt) Algorithm.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/String Searching/KMP (Knuth-Morris-Pratt) Algorithm.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">KMP (Knuth-Morris-Pratt) Algorithm</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What are hash collisions and how do we handle them?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A collision is when two different strings produce the same hash. Rabin-Karp handles this by verifying the actual substring when a hash match occurs, and collisions can be made very unlikely with good moduli/base choices (or double hashing).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/String Searching/Rabit Karp Search.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Algorithms/String Searching/Rabit Karp Search.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Rabit Karp Search</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h2 id="02-computer-science-data-structures">Data Structures</h2><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a data structure? Which ones do you know? Which of them exist in .NET?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A data structure is a way to organize related data into a collection-like object. Examples include arrays, lists, queues, stacks, linked lists, dictionaries/hash tables, hash sets, graphs, and trees. .NET provides built-in implementations for many of these (for example <code>Array</code>, <code>List&lt;T&gt;</code>, <code>Queue&lt;T&gt;</code>, <code>Stack&lt;T&gt;</code>, <code>LinkedList&lt;T&gt;</code>, <code>Dictionary&lt;TKey, TValue&gt;</code>, <code>HashSet&lt;T&gt;</code>).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Data Structures.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Data Structures.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Data Structures</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How is <code>List&lt;T&gt;</code> implemented under the hood?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>List&lt;T&gt;</code> wraps an internal <code>T[]</code> buffer and tracks <code>Count</code> separately from <code>Capacity</code>.<br>
When capacity is exceeded, it allocates a bigger array and copies elements.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/List.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/List.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">List</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between <code>Count</code> and <code>Capacity</code> in <code>List&lt;T&gt;</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>Count</code> is the number of logical elements. <code>Capacity</code> is the size of the internal array.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/List.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/List.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">List</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do <code>Clear()</code> and <code>Remove()</code> affect <code>Capacity</code> in <code>List&lt;T&gt;</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">They usually change only <code>Count</code>. To shrink memory, use <code>TrimExcess()</code> or set <code>Capacity</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/List.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/List.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">List</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What data structure is used behind <code>Dictionary&lt;TKey, TValue&gt;</code>?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A hash table with bucket-based key distribution and collision handling.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Dictionary.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Dictionary.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Dictionary</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is <code>Dictionary</code> usually faster than <code>List</code> for lookups?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">It computes a hash and jumps to a bucket instead of scanning each element.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Dictionary.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Dictionary.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Dictionary</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How does hash collision affect performance?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">More collisions increase comparisons in a bucket chain and can push operations toward O(n).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Dictionary.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Dictionary.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Dictionary</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How does inserting a value into a hashtable work?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">The key is hashed, mapped to a bucket, and inserted there. Collisions are handled by chain/probe resolution.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Hashtable.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Hashtable.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Hashtable</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does using a hash code instead of comparing full keys speed up lookups?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Hashing narrows search to one bucket instead of scanning all entries.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Hashtable.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Hashtable.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Hashtable</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between <code>HashSet&lt;T&gt;</code> and <code>List&lt;T&gt;</code> for membership checks?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>HashSet&lt;T&gt;.Contains</code> is O(1) average; <code>List&lt;T&gt;.Contains</code> is O(n).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/HashSet.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/HashSet.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">HashSet</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why can <code>HashSet&lt;T&gt;.Contains</code> fail for logically equal objects?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because hash/equality contracts are broken (for example, mismatched <code>GetHashCode</code>).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/HashSet.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/HashSet.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">HashSet</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Which built-in .NET collection is closest to a self-balancing tree?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>SortedSet&lt;T&gt;</code> (and <code>SortedDictionary&lt;TKey, TValue&gt;</code> for key-value scenarios).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Trees.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Trees.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Trees</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When would you avoid recursive tree traversal?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">On unknown/deep depth, where iterative traversal with an explicit stack is safer.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Trees.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Trees.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Trees</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Does .NET provide a built-in <code>Graph&lt;T&gt;</code> type?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">No. You usually build graphs using <code>Dictionary</code>, <code>List</code>, <code>HashSet</code>, and <code>Queue</code>/<code>Stack</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Graph.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Graph.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Graph</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Which collections are typically used for BFS?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>Queue&lt;T&gt;</code> for frontier and <code>HashSet&lt;T&gt;</code> for visited tracking.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Graph.md" href="Software Engineering/02 Computer Science/Data Structures/Graph.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Graph</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h1 id="03-data-persistence">03 Data Persistence</h1><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a database?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A database is an organized collection of data stored in a structured way so it can be efficiently created, read, updated, and deleted. In practice you interact with it through a DBMS (Database Management System), which provides storage, indexing, querying, transactions, security, backups, etc.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/03 Data Persistence.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/03 Data Persistence.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">03 Data Persistence</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What are the main types of databases?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Common categories are: relational (SQL tables), key-value, document, wide-column, graph, time-series, and search engines. They differ in data model, query capabilities, consistency guarantees, and scaling approach.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/03 Data Persistence.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/03 Data Persistence.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">03 Data Persistence</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What makes caching hard?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Invalidation and correctness.<br>
You need a clear staleness contract and safe fallbacks.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do you reduce cache stampede?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Add jitter to expirations, use request coalescing, and consider background refresh.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">You cache user profiles in Redis and a user updates their display name then immediately refreshes the page and still sees the old value sometimes. How do you fix it without turning off caching?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Define the correctness target first: read your writes for the updating user, plus a staleness budget for everyone else</li>
<li dir="auto">On the write path, either update the cached value or delete it after the database commit succeeds</li>
<li dir="auto">If there are multiple writers or async pipelines, publish an invalidation event and consume it in all app instances</li>
<li dir="auto">For per user read your writes, use a version token in the cache key, for example row version or updated at, so the writer reads the new version immediately</li>
<li dir="auto">Keep a TTL as a safety net for missed invalidations</li>
<li dir="auto">Add monitoring: rate of stale reads, invalidation lag, and cache hit ratio per key type<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Your API uses TTL only caching with a five minute TTL. At every five minute boundary, p99 latency spikes and the database CPU pegs. What changes do you make?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Add jitter to TTL so expirations spread over time</li>
<li dir="auto">Add request coalescing so only one request recomputes a key and others await the same result</li>
<li dir="auto">Consider stale while revalidate so you never block on recomputation for hot keys</li>
<li dir="auto">Add a short circuit to protect the database: rate limit recomputes, timeouts, and fallback behavior</li>
<li dir="auto">Identify and treat hot keys separately: shorter payloads, proactive refresh, dedicated cache region<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">You run multi tenant SaaS and cache search results. A customer reports seeing another tenant data once. What do you look for and how do you prevent it?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Assume a cache key correctness bug until proven otherwise: ensure tenant id and auth scope are part of every key</li>
<li dir="auto">Verify there is no shared key for different query parameters, locale, feature flags, or permissions</li>
<li dir="auto">Ensure you do not cache error pages or partial failures that can later be served as valid results</li>
<li dir="auto">Use strongly typed key builders and centralized key composition to prevent ad hoc string keys</li>
<li dir="auto">Add defense in depth: validate tenant on deserialized payload before returning and log violations<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Explain ACID</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">ACID describes key transaction guarantees:</p>
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Atomicity: all operations in a transaction succeed or none do.</li>
<li dir="auto">Consistency: committed transactions move the database between valid states (respecting constraints).</li>
<li dir="auto">Isolation: concurrent transactions do not observe each other's intermediate states (controlled by isolation levels).</li>
<li dir="auto">Durability: once committed, data survives crashes (via logging, checkpoints, replication, etc.).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ACID.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ACID.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ACID</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><h2 id="03-data-persistence-nosql">NoSQL</h2><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What are non-relational databases?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Non-relational databases (often grouped under the term NoSQL) store and query data without the classic relational model of normalized tables and joins. They typically favor flexible schemas and horizontal scaling, and come in several major families: key-value, document, wide-column, and graph databases.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/NoSQL/NoSQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/NoSQL/NoSQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">NoSQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">You are building a user profile API with very frequent reads by user id. Which NoSQL family fits best and why?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Key value or document store.<br>
Use key value if the access pattern is almost entirely by id and you do not need rich querying.<br>
Use document store if you need to read and update an aggregate document (profile + preferences) and occasionally query by a few indexed fields.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/NoSQL/NoSQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/NoSQL/NoSQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">NoSQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When is NoSQL a bad idea?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When your core use case needs relational constraints and multi-entity transactions, or your queries are fundamentally join heavy.<br>
In that case, add caching, read replicas, or a denormalized read model before switching storage models.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/NoSQL/NoSQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/NoSQL/NoSQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">NoSQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h2 id="03-data-persistence-orms">ORMs</h2><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How to choose Code First vs Database First?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use Code First when you want the code model to be the source of truth (new projects, strong domain model, migrations as part of delivery). Use Database First when you already have a database schema you must integrate with (legacy DB, shared DB, strict DBA-controlled schema) and want to generate the model from it.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/Entity Framework.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/Entity Framework.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Entity Framework</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What inheritance mapping strategies exist in Entity Framework?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">The common strategies are: TPH (Table Per Hierarchy, single table with a discriminator), TPT (Table Per Type, separate table per type), and TPC (Table Per Concrete type, separate table per concrete type). They trade off query simplicity, normalization, and performance.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/Entity Framework.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/Entity Framework.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Entity Framework</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do you do a backward-compatible schema migration with zero downtime (expand-contract, backfill, dual reads/writes), and what can go wrong?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use an expand-contract migration:<br>
add new schema elements in a backward-compatible way (nullable columns/tables/indexes), deploy code that writes to both old and new (or writes new while keeping old readable), then backfill in batches.<br>
Switch reads behind a feature flag when data is consistent, keep a fallback path temporarily, and only then contract (remove old columns) once all writers/readers are updated.<br>
Failure modes: wrong deploy order, backfill racing with live writes, long-running migrations/locks, missing defaults/null handling, read-model inconsistency, and hard rollbacks after data has diverged.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/Entity Framework.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/Entity Framework.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Entity Framework</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is an ORM?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">An ORM (Object-Relational Mapper) maps relational database tables/rows to objects and translates queries/changes in code into SQL. It helps with CRUD, tracking changes, relationships, and migrations, at the cost of an abstraction layer you must understand to avoid performance issues.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/ORMs.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/ORMs/ORMs.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ORMs</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h2 id="03-data-persistence-sql">SQL</h2><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is an index and what types exist?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">An index is an additional on-disk/in-memory structure (often a B-tree/B+ tree) that speeds up access via seeks and ordered scans. Common types are clustered and nonclustered indexes, plus unique, composite, filtered/partial, and full-text indexes depending on DB engine.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How does ordering work for clustered vs nonclustered indexes?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">In a clustered index, the leaf level is the table data itself, physically ordered by the clustered key. In a nonclustered index, the leaf level is ordered by nonclustered key and stores locators to data rows.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why cannot a table have two clustered indexes?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A clustered index defines physical row order. One table can be physically ordered only one way at a time.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">If clustered tables are often faster for reads, why would you still use a heap?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use this for bulk-load/staging scenarios and append-heavy transient data where ordered access is not required.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do fill factor and page splits affect write performance?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Lower fill factor leaves room on pages and can reduce splits, but increases storage and read IO.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Can a clustered index key contain duplicates?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Yes. SQL Server makes keys unique internally by adding a hidden uniquifier when needed.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How are rows located from a nonclustered index when the base table is a heap?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">The nonclustered leaf stores a RID pointing to file/page/slot.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why not index every column?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Extra indexes increase write cost, memory pressure, and maintenance; some low-selectivity indexes are not useful.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Do you always make the primary key clustered?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">No. It is common, but choose clustered key by access patterns, size, and update behavior.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between composite and covering indexes?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Composite defines key columns used for seek/order. Covering also includes non-key columns to avoid lookups.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Can you index only a subset of rows?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Yes, with filtered indexes (where supported by engine).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/Indexes.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Indexes</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is normalization? What are its first three normal forms?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Answer is not provided in the source interview list; see Links.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is denormalization? When is it useful?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Answer is not provided in the source interview list; see Links.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the logical SQL query execution order?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ol>
<li dir="auto">FROM</li>
<li dir="auto">ON</li>
<li dir="auto">JOIN</li>
<li dir="auto">WHERE</li>
<li dir="auto">GROUP BY</li>
<li dir="auto">WITH CUBE or WITH ROLLUP</li>
<li dir="auto">HAVING</li>
<li dir="auto">SELECT</li>
<li dir="auto">DISTINCT</li>
<li dir="auto">ORDER BY</li>
<li dir="auto">TOP<br>
A common logical order is: <code>FROM</code> (incl. <code>JOIN</code>/<code>ON</code>) -&gt; <code>WHERE</code> -&gt; <code>GROUP BY</code> -&gt; <code>HAVING</code> -&gt; <code>SELECT</code> -&gt; <code>DISTINCT</code> -&gt; <code>ORDER BY</code> -&gt; <code>TOP</code>/<code>LIMIT</code>/<code>OFFSET</code> (exact details vary by engine).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></li>
</ol>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">In what structure is data stored in SQL?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">In the relational model, data is stored as relations: tables with columns (attributes) and rows (tuples). Tables are grouped into schemas/databases, and relationships are represented via keys (primary/foreign) rather than by nesting objects.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a primary key?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A primary key is a constraint that uniquely identifies each row in a table. It must be unique and not null, can be single-column or composite, and is typically backed by an index (implementation depends on the DB engine).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a foreign key?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A foreign key is a constraint that enforces a relationship between tables by requiring values in one table to reference existing values in a primary/unique key of another table. It protects referential integrity and can define cascading actions on update/delete.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a unique key?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A unique key (UNIQUE constraint) enforces that values in a column (or set of columns) are unique across the table. Unlike a primary key, a table can have multiple unique constraints; null handling varies by DB engine.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What table constraints exist?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Typical constraints include: <code>NOT NULL</code>, <code>CHECK</code>, <code>DEFAULT</code>, <code>UNIQUE</code>, <code>PRIMARY KEY</code>, and <code>FOREIGN KEY</code>. They are used to enforce domain rules, uniqueness, and referential integrity at the database level.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What JOIN types exist?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Common JOINs are: <code>INNER JOIN</code>, <code>LEFT OUTER JOIN</code>, <code>RIGHT OUTER JOIN</code>, <code>FULL OUTER JOIN</code>, and <code>CROSS JOIN</code>. A self-join is when you join a table to itself; semi/anti joins are often expressed via <code>EXISTS</code>/<code>NOT EXISTS</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What does DISTINCT do?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>DISTINCT</code> removes duplicate rows from the result set (uniqueness is evaluated across the selected columns). It is applied after <code>SELECT</code> projection in the logical processing order.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between WHERE and HAVING?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>WHERE</code> filters rows before grouping/aggregation. <code>HAVING</code> filters groups after <code>GROUP BY</code> and can use aggregate expressions like <code>COUNT(*)</code> or <code>SUM(amount)</code>.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the difference between CHAR and VARCHAR?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto"><code>CHAR(n)</code> is fixed-length: values are padded to length <code>n</code>. <code>VARCHAR(n)</code> is variable-length: it stores only the actual length (plus small overhead). Use <code>NCHAR</code>/<code>NVARCHAR</code> when you need Unicode (engine-specific).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a stored procedure and how is it different from a function?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A stored procedure is server-side code stored in the database and executed by name; it can encapsulate multi-step logic, perform data modifications, and return result sets. Functions usually return a value (scalar/table) and are often more restricted in side effects (varies by DB engine).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is a trigger?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A trigger is database code that automatically runs in response to events (e.g., <code>INSERT</code>, <code>UPDATE</code>, <code>DELETE</code>, sometimes DDL events). It is commonly used for enforcing rules, auditing, and maintaining derived data.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" href="Software Engineering/03 Data Persistence/SQL/SQL.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">SQL</a></em></p>
